тАШ рдкреНрд░ рд╢реНрдпрд╛рд╡рд╛рд╢реНрд╡ ’ рдЗрддрд┐ рд╕рдкреНрддрджрд╢рд░реНрдЪрдорд╖реНрдЯрдордВ рд╕реВрдХреНрддрдореН ред рдЕрддреНрд░реЗрдпрдордиреБрдХреНрд░рдордгрд┐рдХрд╛ тАУ’ рдкреНрд░ рд╢реНрдпрд╛рд╡рд╛рд╢реНрд╡ рддреНрд░реНрдпреВрдирд╛ рд╢реНрдпрд╛рд╡рд╛рд╢реНрд╡реЛ рдорд╛рд░реБрддрдВ рд╣ рддрддреНрдкрдЩреНрдХреНрддрд┐рдГ рд╖рд╖реНрдареНрдпрдиреНрддреНрдпрд╛ рдЪ ’ рдЗрддрд┐ ред рдЖрддреНрд░реЗрдпрдГ рд╢реНрдпрд╛рд╡рд╛рд╢реНрд╡ рдЛрд╖рд┐рдГ ред тАШрд╣ рддрддреН’ рдЗрддрд┐ рдкреНрд░рдпреЛрдЧрд╛рддреН рдЗрджрдорд╛рджреАрдирд┐ рджрд╢ рд╕реВрдХреНрддрд╛рдирд┐ рдорд░реБрджреНрджреЗрд╡рддреНрдпрд╛рдирд┐ ред рд╖рд╖реНрдареА рд╕рдкреНрддрджрд╢реА рдЪ рдкрдЩреНрдХреНрддреНрдпреМ рд╢рд┐рд╖реНрдЯрд╛рдГ рдкрдЩреНрдХреНрддреНрдпрдиреНрддрдкрд░рд┐рднрд╛рд╖рдпрд╛рдиреБрд╖реНрдЯреБрднрдГ ред рдЧрддреЛ рд╡рд┐рдирд┐рдпреЛрдЧрдГ рее

Jamison Brereton

52 (406)
Maruts
┼Ъy─Бv─Б┼Ыva ─Аtreya
17 verses: anuс╣гс╣нubh, except paс╣Еkti 6, 16тАУ17
As befits the first hymn in this Marut cycle, the poet ┼Ъy─Бv─Б┼Ыva addresses himself with an exhortation to praise the Maruts in the first p─Бda of the first verse. He then

describes them in a general fashion and asserts their right to the sacrifice, in a short ring-compositional introduction (vss. 1тАУ5). (For the responsions of verses 1 and 5 as an example of тАЬpoetic repair,тАЭ see Jamison 2006.)
The next section of the hymn (vss. 6тАУ13) depicts the Maruts as the gods of the thunderstorm in a series of vivid images and also fancifully assigns individual names to them (vss. 10тАУ11)тАФthe Maruts are otherwise undifferentiatedтАФending with another exhortation to the poet to praise them (vs. 13cd). In the last few verses (14тАУ17) ritual honor is given to the Maruts, and they respond with gifts. The last verse (17) resembles a d─Бnastuti, but with the Maruts, rather than humans, as the donors to the poet; they were already identified as тАЬpatronsтАЭ (s┼лr├н) in the two pre
ceding verses (15тАУ16).
The density of imagery throughout is remarkable; we will give just one example, from verse 9. There the Maruts are said to тАЬclothe themselves in wool in the Paruс╣гс╣З─л River.тАЭ The тАЬwoolтАЭ must stand for foam, off-white and fluffy like newly shorn wool. But the river foam is yet another metaphorical substitute for something else, namely clouds, which the Maruts as storm gods would be clothed inтАФall of this conveyed in an economical half-verse.

Jamison Brereton Notes

Maruts The pattern of the mention of the MarutsтАЩ name in this hymn is worth noting: it might be called a тАЬversified paradigmтАЭ (├а la I.1) with a hole in it. The various oblique forms of the plural stem mar├║t- are densely clustered at the beginning of the hymn: instr. mar├║dbhiс╕е (1b), gen. mar├║t─Бm (3c), loc. mar├║tsu (4a), dat. mar├║dbhyaс╕е (5d), and acc. mar├║taс╕е (6d) – each oblique case represented (if abl. is lumped with dat.), each once only. In addition there are three forms of the vс╣Ыddhied m─Б╠Бrutam in the neut. acc. sg. later in the hymn (8a, 13c, 14a). However, though these gods are frequently referred to in the nom. pl. in the hymn, beginning with y├й in 1c, and once in the voc. (dhс╣Ыс╣гс╣Зavaс╕е 14c), there are no forms of the nom. mar├║taс╕е or the voc. m├бrutaс╕е / marutaс╕е, although these are the most common forms of this stem in the RV. After the paradigm has been established in the early part of the hymn (1-6), there are no further occurrences of the simple stem in the 11 remaining vss. (7-17), only the three vс╣Ыddhi forms. I donтАЩt know what, if anything, to make of this, but it does not seem by chance.

On the responsions and ring-compositional structure of vss. 1-5, see the published

introduction. and my тАЬPoetic тАШRepairтАЩ in the Rig VedaтАЭ (2006: 133-36), as well as The Rigveda between Two Worlds (2007: 112-13). The responsions and the versified paradigm are most likely related; as I argue in тАЬPoetic тАШRepairтАЩтАЭ the instr. in the phrase ├бrc─Б mar├║dbhiс╕е тАж in vs. 1 is somewhat anomalous, but it is тАЬrepairedтАЭ by the substitution of the expected dat. in 5d тАж arc─Б mar├║dbhyaс╕е. To summarize those discussions briefly, in a hymn devoted to the Maruts, beginning with the selfexhortation of the poet тАЬchant forth,тАЭ we might expect the Maruts to be the recipients (dat.) of the chant, not, as it seems, fellow-chanters (instr.) with the human poet. But putting them in the instr. emphasizes an important part of their profile, that they are also known to chant, a feature that is alluded to by the hemistich-final adj. с╣Ы╠Бkvabhiс╕е тАШpossessing the chantтАЩ. Thus the beginning of the hymn seems concerned with the MarutsтАЩ contrastive and mediating functional roles as expressed by the oblique cases of the paradigm.

рд╣реЗ рд╢реНрдпрд╛рд╡рд╛рд╢реНрд╡ рдПрддрдиреНрдирд╛рдордХ рдЛрд╖реЗ рдзреГрд╖реНрдгреБрдпрд╛ рдзреГрд╖реНрдгреБрд╕реНрддреНрд╡рдореН рдЛрдХреНрд╡рднрд┐рдГ рд╕реНрддреБрддреНрдпрд╛рдиреН рдорд░реБрджреНрднрд┐рдГ рдорд░реБрддрдГ рдкреНрд░ рдЕрд░реНрдЪ ред рджреНрд╡рд┐рддреАрдпрд╛рд░реНрдереЗ рддреГрддреАрдпрд╛ ред рдПрд╡рдВ рд╕реНрд╡рдпрдореЗрд╡ рд╕рдВрдкреНрд░реЗрд╖реНрдпрддрд┐ ред рдпрджреНрд╡рд╛ ред рдпрдЬрдорд╛рдиреЛ рд╣реЛрддрд╛рд░рдВ рд╢реНрдпрд╛рд╡рд╛рд╢реНрд╡рдВ рдмреНрд░реВрддреЗ ред рдпрджреНрд╡рд╛ ред рдорд░реБрджреНрднрд┐рд░реНрдорд░реБрддреНрд╕рджреГрд╢реИрд░реНрдЛрдХреНрд╡рднрд┐рдГ рд╕реНрддреЛрддреГрднрд┐рдГ рд╕рд╣ рд╕реНрддреЛрддреНрд░реИрд░реНрд╡рд╛ рдЕрд░реНрдЪ рд╕реНрддреБрд╣реАрддреНрдпрд░реНрдердГ ред рдпреЗ рдорд░реБрддрдГ рдпрдЬреНрдЮрд┐рдпрд╛рдГ рдпрдЬреНрдЮрд╛рд░реНрд╣рд╛рдГ рдЕрдиреБрд╖реНрд╡рдзрдВ рдкреНрд░рддреНрдпрд╣рдореНред рд╣рд╡рд┐рд░реНрд▓рдХреНрд╖рдгрд╛рдиреНрдирдкреНрд░рджрд╛рдирдВ рд╕реНрд╡рдзрд╛ ред рдЕрдиреБ рдкрд╢реНрдЪрд╛рджреНрд╡рд╛ ред рдЕрджреНрд░реЛрдШрдореН рдЕрд╣рд┐рдВрд╕рдХрдВ рд╢реНрд░рд╡рдГ рдЕрдиреНрдирдВ рд▓рдмреНрдзреНрд╡рд╛ рдорджрдиреНрддрд┐ рд╣реГрд╖реНрдпрдиреНрддрд┐ рее

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬOffer, worship with person verance, ┼Ъy─Бv─Б┼Ыva, to the praise-deserving Maruts; they who are adorable and delight in the daily offered and inoffensive sacrificial food.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

┼Ъy─Бv─Б┼Ыva, chant forth boldlyтАФalong with the Maruts possessing chants, who rejoice in [/cheer on] undisguised fame according to their own
nature, those worthy of the sacrifice.

Jamison Brereton Notes

On the somewhat anomalous expression in the first hemistich, see reff. given just above.

The 2nd hemistich is also syntactically somewhat compromised. Forms of uncompounded тИЪmad that mean тАШtake pleasure in / enjoyтАЩ seldom if ever (possibly VII.49.4) take the acc. (as also noted by Renou), in preference to instr., gen., or loc.; yet m├бdanti here seems to take acc. ┼Ыr├бvaс╕е as obj. It might be possible to extract ├бnu from the cmpd anuс╣гvadh├бm тАШaccording to their own natureтАЩ and construe it with m├бdanti, since ├бnu тИЪmad тАШcheer onтАЩ does take an acc. – but a personal acc., not the neut. inanimate тАШfameтАЩ that it would govern here. So an unresolvable syntactic tension has been set up. I think the tension reflects the double role of the Maruts already encountered in p─Бda b. As recipients of ┼Ъy─Бv─Б┼ЫvaтАЩs praise chant, they would тАЬtake pleasure in their fame,тАЭ but as participants in the chanting they would тАЬcheer onтАЭ the fame of other(s).

Geldner and Renou seem to take adrogh├бm as an adv., a possibility also mentioned by Witzel Got┼Н. However, the other apparent adv. form has initial accent (├бdrogham VIII.60.4), and furthermore the existence of a bahuvr─лhi ├бdrogha-v─Бc- (2x) and the syntagm adrogh├б- v├бcas- (III.14.6) support a collocation with semantically similar ┼Ыr├бvas-.

Griffith

SING boldly forth, Syavasva, with the Maruts who are loud in song,
Who, holy, as their wont is, joy in glory that is free from guile.

Geldner

Syavasva! Stimme zuversichtlich mit den singenden Marut das Lied an, die ohne Falsch nach ihrer Art sich am Ruhm berauschen, die Opferw├╝rdigen.

Grassmann

Auf, ├Зjavaa├зva, stimme k├╝hn in den Gesang der Maruts ein, Die treugesinnt aus eigner Lust, des Ruhms sich freu’n, die heiligen.

Elizarenkova

English translation:

тАЬThey are the firm friends of steady vigour, who, proceeding resolute on their way, willingly protect (our) numerous (descendants).тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

For they are comrades of steadfast strengthтАФboldly.
Bold on their drive, by themselves they protect each and every one.

Jamison Brereton Notes

It is not clear why the rel. cl. of ab contains s├бnti, as the clause seems a simple equational one (тАЬsince they are comradesтАЭ), and such clauses generally lack an overt copula. Geldner takes dhс╣Ыс╣гс╣Зuy─Б╠Бas a predication with s├бnti, as, it seems, do Witzel Got┼Н.

This is in principle appealing, but given that we get untethered adv. dhс╣Ыс╣гnuy─Б╠Бin the previous and following vss. (1a, 4b) and a similar equational (rel.) cl. in 13ab (y├й тАж kav├бyaс╕е s├бnti тАЬwho are poets,тАЭ it does not seem compelling.

Geldner takes dhс╣Ыс╣гadv├нnaс╕е as acc. pl. with ┼Ы├б┼Ыvataс╕е, but he seems isolated in this interpr., starting from S─Бyaс╣Зa., who takes it as the nom. pl. that otherwise universally prevails.

English translation:

тАЬGliding along, and shedding moisture, they pass through the nights; therefore we now celebrate the might of the Maruts, manifested in both heaven and earth.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

They, like streaming bulls, spring across the nights.
Then the MarutsтАЩ might in heaven and earth we ponder.

Jamison Brereton Notes

As Geldner points out, the verb ├бti тИЪskand тАШspring across/beyondтАЩ is reminiscent of ├бdhi тИЪskand, which refers to sexual mounting. He supplies a parenthetical тАЬ(auf die K├╝he)тАЭ in the simile (so also Renou), and I would now also do so: тАЬthey spring across the nights, as streaming bulls spring (upon cows).тАЭ The meaning тАШnightтАЩ for the rare and etymologically unclear (see EWA s.v.; also Witzel Got┼Н n., with more confidence in the etym.) ┼Ы├бrvar─л- seems established by later Vedic and MIA evidence, but I do not know why the word appears in this passage. A fem. word for night is necessary to make the implicit sexual pun work, but the better attested r─Б╠Бtr─л- is of course also fem. It somewhat responds phonologically to likewise p─Бda-final ┼Ы├б┼Ыvataс╕е in 3b, and it therefore might form a web, along with syand(r─Б╠Бsaс╕е) тАж с╣гkand(anti) earlier in the hemistich – but the phonological connections seem too slight. Maybe ┼Ъy─Бv─Б┼Ыva just likes words that begin with his initial.

I am not certain what image is being conveyed. Geldner suggests that the MarutsтАЩ storms calm down at night and then take on renewed energy in the morning, but the two passages he adduces donтАЩt seem to support that interpr. Moreover, тАШspring across/beyondтАЩ seems to me the opposite of what Geldner envisions: itтАЩs a vigorous action not a relaxation into tranquility. I tentatively suggest that it refers to the fact that thunderstorms (or, rather, the associated lightning flashes) are especially visible at night and appear to streak across the dark sky.

Griffith

Like steers in rapid motion they advance and overtake the nights;
And thus the Maruts’ power in heaven and on the earth we celebrate.

Geldner

Sie springen ├╝ber die N├дchte weg wie die sprunglustigen Stiere auf die K├╝he. Dann gedenken wir der Macht der Marut im Himmel und auf Erden.

Grassmann

Den aufgeregten Stieren gleich bespringen ihre Schecken sie, Drum denken an der Maruts Macht im Himmel und auf Erden wir.

Elizarenkova

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬOffer sacrifice to the adorable Maruts, who (have come) from heaven, who are worthy of worship, munificent leaders (of rites), and possessors of unequalled strength.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

The deserving ones possessing good drops [/gifts], men who are not half-strength,
to the Maruts of heaven chant forthтАФ(chant) a sacrifice for those worthy of the sacrifice.

Jamison Brereton Notes

This is the vs. in which the problematic instr. of 1b is resolved – тАЬrepairedтАЭ -

  • but, as discussed in my 2006 paper, the poet produces a new conundrum, though this one can be, as it were, pre-repaired. The obj. yaj├▒├бm тАШsacrificeтАЩ is unexpected with the verb pr├б тАж arc─Б тАШchant forthтАЩ; we expect a verbal product as object. But the yaj├▒├бm here is picking up the conjoined phrase st├│maс╣Г yaj├▒├бс╣Г ca of 4b, whose st├│mam would be an appropriate obj. of pr├б тАж arc─Б.
Griffith

Praiseworthy, givers of good gifts, Heroes with full and perfect strength -
To Maruts, Holy Ones of heaven, will I extol the sacrifice.

Geldner

Die w├╝rdig sind, Freigebige zu hei├Яen, M├дnner von ganzer Kraft, den opferwerten Mannen des Himmels, den Marut, stimme das Opfergebet an!

Grassmann

Den M├дnnern preis das Opfer an, was den zu ehrenden geb├╝hrt, Die reichlich regnen stark an Kraft, den Maruts, die vom Himmel sind.

Elizarenkova

English translation:

тАЬLeaders (of the rains), the mighty Maruts shine with brilliant ornaments and weapons, and hurl javelin (at their foes, the clouds); the lightnings like roaring (torrents), daily follow the Maruts; the radiance of the resplendent (cohort) spontaneously breaks forth.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

(Arrived) here with brilliants, here with battle, the lofty men have launched their spears.
Following them (came) the lightning flashesтАФfollowing the Maruts like giggling (girls). The radiance of heaven has arrived by itself.

Jamison Brereton Notes

This vs. is in Paс╣Еkti; that is, it contains five 8-syllable p─Бdas rather than the four of Anuс╣гс╣нubh, otherwise the meter of the hymn until the end, where the final two vss. are also in Paс╣Еkti. Here the slight shift in meter seems to mark a boundary: on the one hand it brings the versified paradigm to a close, with the acc. mar├║taс╕е in d; on the other it announces the advent of the gods with their storms and inaugurates the descriptive passages that dominate the remainder of the hymn.

The first p─Бda lacks a verb; Geldner makes a valiant effort to construe asс╣Ыkс╣гata of b with p─Бda a as well, in two different senses (see his n. 6; тАШтАж sind тАж herangesprengtтАЩ for a, тАШhaben тАж geschleudertтАЩ for b), but the former would be a unique sense for ─Б╠Б тИЪsс╣Ыj. Grassmann also invents a unique sense тАШdecorate X with YтАЩ to allow the two p─Бdas to be construed as a single construction. To avoid such ad hoc contrivances it seems best to follow Oldenberg in supplying a verb of motion with the insistent ─Б╠Бin p─Бda a.

The adj. that begins p─Бda b, с╣Ы┼Ыv─Б╠Б(с╕е), can be either acc. pl. fem. modifying с╣Ыс╣гс╣н─л╠Бс╕е тАШspearsтАЩ (so Grassmann, apparently also Witzel Got┼Н) or nom. pl. masc. modifying n├бra(с╕е) тАШmenтАЩ.

The p─Бda break preceding it might favor the former interpr., but 13a, where the Maruts are definitely called с╣Ыс╣гv─Б╠Б(с╕е), favors the latter, esp. since the Maruts are also с╣Ыс╣гv├б- elsewhere (e.g., I.64.2). Note that in 13a the adj. is also followed by тАШspearтАЩ, but safely bound in a cmpd: с╣Ыс╣гv─Б╠Бс╣Ыс╣гс╣н├нvidyutaс╕е; this bahuvr─лhi тАШwhose spears are lightning flashesтАЩ combines the independent words с╣Ыс╣гс╣н─л╠Бс╕е and vidy├║taс╕е of our vs. (p─Бdas b and c respectively) and enforces their identity. This resolution in 13a of the ambiguity of 6ab can be seen as another example of тАЬrepair.тАЭ Partly because the poet seems to be drawing attention to the phrase by resolving it in 13a I am now inclined to take с╣Ыс╣гv─Б╠Б(с╕е) in 6b with both of its possible referents and emend the tr. to тАЬthe lofty men have launched their spears aloft.тАЭ It would be one of the reasonably many examples where a grammatically ambiguous descripter is positioned exactly between its two possible referents.

The hapax fem. part. j├бjjhat─лс╕е тАШgigglingтАЩ is, of course, phonologically quite striking. As discussed by Hoffmann (Aufs. 306 and n. 3 = KZ 83 [1969]), the form is based on the redupl. pres. to тИЪhas тАШlaughтАЩ with a Middle Indic (тАЬdialectalтАЭ) development of the cluster *gh-s (rather than the expected -kс╣г- found in the masc.

part. to the same redupl. pres. j├бkс╣гat- in I.33.7). The use of such a phonologically exotic word is reminiscent of the equally exotic akhkhal─л- in the frog hymn (VII.103.3). The latter, as Thieme has convincingly argued, is an importation from pedagogical discourse, conducted for young boys in a preform of Middle Indic. Our form here seems adopted from vernacular тАЬwomenтАЩs languageтАЭ and brings a whiff of family life: little girls running after their brothers or parents with little-girl giggles – a life that would, of course, be conducted in a vernacular (pre-) Middle Indic.

P─Бda e has several parallels, given by Geldner in his n. 6e. The question in our passage is whether div├бс╕е is gen., as IтАЩve taken it (so also Geldner and somewhat differently Renou), or abl. (тАЬThe radiance arose … from heavenтАЭ; so Witzel Got┼Н). The parallels cut both ways: V.25.8 sv─Бn├│ arta tm├бn─Б divaс╕е and VII.34.7 ├║d asya ┼Ы├║с╣гm─Бd bh─Бn├║r n─Б╠Бrta seem to favor an abl. interpr., but IV.1.17 ├║d devy─Б╠Бuс╣г├бso bh─Бn├║r arta a genitive. In the end, I donтАЩt think the choice materially affects the sense of the passage: whether the radiance is тАШof heavenтАЩ or тАШfrom heavenтАЩ the result is pretty much the same.

English translation:

тАЬThe Maruts, who are of the earth are augmented, so are those in the vast firmament; they increase in the force of the rivers, and in the aggregate of the spacious heaven.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

The Maruts who are of the earth: ye p─Бrthiv─Б = pс╣Ыthivisambaddhaс╕е, connected with the earth

Jamison Brereton

Those who have grown strong as earthlings, who in the broad midspace, or in the precinct of the rivers, or in the seat of great heavenтАФ

Jamison Brereton Notes

This vs. consists of a single rel. cl. (y├й тАж y├й) with no main cl. It is most probably preposed to vs. 8 with its correlative the neut. sg. ┼Ы├бrdho m─Б╠Бrutam тАЬthe Marut troop,тАЭ despite the mismatch in number and gender. The end of vs. 6 has no reference to the Maruts, and, as I noted above, it serves as a boundary vs. The same structure with number disharmony envisaged here across p─Бda boundary (7a y├й тАж, b y├й тАж // 8a ┼Ы├бrdho m─Б╠Бrutam тАж) is found, more clearly, within a vs. in 13: 13a y├й тАж / 13c t├бm тАж m─Б╠Бrutaс╣Г gaс╣З├бm тАж, perhaps another example of repair.

The usual tripartite division of the cosmos (earth, midspace, heaven) is here complicated by the intrusion of a fourth, тАЬthe precinct of the riversтАЭ (vс╣Ыj├бnanad─л╠Бn─Бm). Renou also notes this, but suggests that c does nothing but тАЬenjoliverтАЭ (embellish) a – that is, that the rivers are a variant of the earth. In a basic sense he is correct, but I would add that what we have here may be the clash of two formulaic expressions of contrastive geographic totality – the standard tripartite model and one, barely attested, in which a nearer or lower vс╣Ыj├бna- is contrasted with something more distant. Cf. esp. I.101.8 (with mention of the Maruts) y├бd v─Б marutvaс╕е param├й sadh├бsthe, y├бd v─Бvam├й vrj├бne m ╠е ─Бdayasva, a bipartite phrase where a seat (sadh├бsthaas here) that is param├б- тАШhigh/distantтАЩ is contrasted with avam├й vс╣Ыj├бne тАШlowest/nearest enclosureтАЩ; a vс╣Ыj├бna- is similarly ├бvare in II.24.11. Thus, though p─Бda c may refer to the same general geographical location as a, namely earth, it also evokes a paired, rather than tripartite, contrast like that in I.101.8 just cited.

The pf. injunc. 3rd pl. v─Бvс╣Ыdh├бnta (see K├╝mmel 471) is attested several times elsewhere and manifestly belongs to a redupl. stem. It is worth noting, however, that the poet seems to be playing with its long reduplication. The v─Б is positioned exactly where we would expect v─Б тАШorтАЩ to be (WackernagelтАЩs position: #y├й v─Бvс╣Ыdh├бnta тАж), anticipating the two v─БтАЩs in p─Бdas c and d, also in WackernagelтАЩs position. I am not suggesting a re-segmentation as v─Б vс╣Ыdh├бnta, simply pointing to ┼Ъy─Бv─Б┼ЫvaтАЩs penchant for verbal play and for making single forms do double duty. To extend this analysis, note the beginning of p─Бda b, ya ur─Б╠Бv тАж, with ─Б╠Бv that could be taken as a metathesis of v─Б.

Griffith

They who waxed mighty, of the earth, they who are in the wide mid-air,
Or in the rivers’ compass, or in the abode of ample heaven.

Die als Erdenbewohner, die im weiten Luftraum oder im Umkreis der Fl├╝sse oder im weiten Raum des gro├Яen Himmels herangewachsen sind.

English translation:

тАЬGlorify the truth-invigorated and infinite strength of the Maruts, for they, the leaders (of the rains), gliding along, are labouring voluntarily for (our) good.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Exalt the Marut troop, of real strength, ingenious.
The men, streaming, hitch up by themselves for beauty.

Jamison Brereton Notes

Geldner takes syandr─Б╠Б(с╕е) as acc. pl. fem. and supplies antelopes as the obj. of yujata. This is not impossible, but syandr─Б╠Б(с╕е) was already used of the Maruts in 3a (cf. also V.87.3).

I don’t understand the force of ut├б sma, which opens 8c and 9a, with ut├б opening 9c. Klein (DGRV I.416-17) says that they introduce parallel statements about the Maruts and represent тАЬconcatenation across the stanza-boundary,тАЭ halfway between intrastanzaic and interstanzaic usage. But the role of sma, whatever it may be, seems downplayed in this description.

English translation:

тАЬWhether they (abide) on the Paruс╣гс╣Зi (river), or, purifying (all), they clothe themselves with light, or whether they break through the clouds with strength by the wheels of their chariots.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Urс╣З─Б vasata ┼Ыundhyavaс╕е = diptiс╕е ┼Ыodhikaс╕е ─Бcch─Бdayanti = purifiers they put on light

Jamison Brereton

And they clothe themselves in wool [=foam] in the Paruс╣гс╣З─л (River)тАФthey (like) preening water-birdsтАФ
and with the wheel-rim of their chariots they split the stone with force.

Jamison Brereton Notes

The phrase p├бruс╣гс╣Зy─Бm ┼л╠Бrс╣З─Б vasata is similar to IV.22.2 p├бruс╣гс╣З─лm uс╣г├бm─Бс╣Зa ┼л╠Бrс╣З─Бm, but while in the latter p├бruс╣гс╣З─лm modifies тАШwoolтАЩ, here it must be a loc. sg.

The тАШwoolтАЩ in both passages is best understood as a metaphor for тАШfoamтАЩ. The stem p├бruс╣гс╣З─л- is the fem. corresponding to paruс╣г├б- тАШgrayтАЩ. It is also a river name, presumably so called because it is covered with grayish foam. For disc. see Oldenberg, Hoffmann (Aufs. 333-35 [=Die Sprache 1974]). The mediating image in this picture is provided by ┼Ыundhy├бvaс╕е; I follow Thieme (KZ 79 [1965] = Kl Sch. 219ff.) in interpr. this form as тАШpreening [waterbird]тАЩ (to тИЪ┼Ыudh тАШcleanтАЩ). As pointed out in the published introduction, the density of imagery is remarkable: the Maruts swathed in clouds (not explicitly mentioned) are compared to birds in a river covered with foam, with the foam (again not explicit) characterized as wool.

The instr. sg. pavy─Б╠Бto the masc. stem pav├н- shows the older -─Б ending, which becomes limited to fem. -i-stems when the masc./ neut. adopt -in─Б.

But the role of sma, whatever it may be, seems downplayed in this description.

рдЖрдкрдердпрдГ ред рдЕрд╕реНрдорджрднрд┐рд╕реБрдЦрд╛ рдорд╛рд░реНрдЧрд╛ рдпреЗрд╖рд╛рдВ рддреЗ рддрд╛рджреГрд╢рд╛рдГ ред рд╡рд┐рдкрдердпрдГ рд╡рд┐рд╖реНрд╡рдЧреНрдорд╛рд░реНрдЧрд╛рдГ рдЕрдиреНрддрд╕реНрдкрдерд╛рдГ рджрд░реАрд╕реБрдЪрд┐рд░рд╛рджрд┐рдорд╛рд░реНрдЧрд╛рдГ рдЕрдиреБрдкрдерд╛рдГ рдЕрдиреБрдХреВрд▓рдорд╛рд░реНрдЧрд╛рд╢реНрдЪ рдпреЗ рдорд░реБрддрдГ рд╕рдиреНрддрд┐ рддреЗ рдПрддреЗрднрд┐рдГ рдПрддреИрд╢реНрдЪрддреБрд░реНрд╡рд┐рдзреИрдГ рдирд╛рдорднрд┐рдГ рдирд╛рдордХреИрдГ рд╕реНрд╡рд░реВрдкреИрдГ рдорд╣реНрдпрдВ рдорджрд░реНрдердВ рдпрдЬреНрдЮрдВ рд╡рд┐рд╕реНрддрд╛рд░рдГ рд╡рд┐рд╕реНрддреГрддрд╛рдГ рд╕рдиреНрддрдГ рдУрд╣рддреЗ рд╡рд╣рдиреНрддрд┐ ред рдпрджреНрд╡рд╛ ред рдПрддреИрд░реНрдирд╛рдорднрд┐рд░реБрджрдХреИрдГ рд╕рд╛рд░реНрдзрдВ рдпрдЬреНрдЮрдореЛрд╣рддреЗ рее рее реп рее

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬ(Whether), following the paths that lead (to us), or that spread diversely, or those that sink into the hollows (of the mountain), or those that extend smoothly, they, (however) scattered, accept the sacrifice for my benefit, (when invoked by these appellations).тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

The paths that lead us: ─Бpathayaс╕е vipathayaс╕е antaspath─Бс╕е anupath─Бс╕е: may also be considered as the proper names of these four orders of the Maruts

Jamison Brereton

тАЬOn the Path,тАЭ тАЬOff the Path,тАЭ тАЬWithin the Path,тАЭ тАЬAlong the PathтАЭтАФ with these names they vaunt themselves to me at the bestrewing of the sacrifice.

Jamison Brereton Notes

The first half-vs. consists of fanciful names of the individual Maruts (never otherwise named), summed up with the instr. phrase et├йbhiс╕е тАж n─Б╠Бmabhiс╕е тАЬwith these namesтАЭ in c. The rest of the second hemistich is unclear, however, primarily because the formal identity and meaning of ohate are disputed. The former issue is the easier to solve: though Grassmann identifies the verb as a 3rd sg. and Renou hesitates, it must be a 3rd pl. to the root pres. (of тИЪoh/uh) (see EWA s.v. OH and esp. Narten [Kl Sch.

98-100 =1969]). The basis for considering it a 3rd sg. is the PpтАЩs interpr. of viс╣гс╣н─Бr├б as nom. sg. viс╣гс╣н─Бr├бс╕е, but a loc. sg. in -├й is equally possible. It is highly unlikely that ohate would be 3rd singular in 10d but 3rd plural in 11a, b, as Grassmann, for ex., takes them.

The questions then are who is the subj. and how does the verb fit with the rest of the material in the half-verse. Most interpr. take yaj├▒├бm as the obj. and tr. тАЬpraise the sacrifice,тАЭ with either the Maruts or unidentified priests/poets as subj. This is not impossible, but given the two ohate in the next vs., which lack objects (unless yaj├▒├бm is supplied, so, e.g., Grassmann), I prefer to seek a consistent interpr. of the verb forms. The root is used on a number of occasions as a passive тАШbe laudedтАЩ / reflexive тАШvaunt oneselfтАЩ (cf., e.g., V.30.6, VIII.5.39). Here I take the Maruts as subject and the names in ab to be the verbal content of the MarutsтАЩ vaunt. (Note that the threefold repetition of ohate here is matched by the three occurrences of vocanta in vs. 16, also with the Maruts as subj.) Under this interpr. the dat. m├бhyam, which is problematic in most interpr., expresses the verbal recipient of the boast. This leaves yaj├▒├бm viс╣гс╣н─Бr├й. For most interpr. the latter word characterizes the Maruts as they come to the sacrifice – e.g., Geldner тАШin breiter ScharтАЩ. Again, not impossible. However, the root тИЪstс╣Ы тАШstrewтАЩ is almost always closely associated with the ritual, esp. with the strewing of the barhis, and I suggest that viс╣гс╣н─Бr├й is a infinitival locative that takes verbal rection, hence тАЬat the bestrewing of the sacrifice.тАЭ However, I realize that this interpr. has some problems: -st─Бr├й is an unlikely infinitival form, and тИЪstс╣Ы doesnтАЩt elsewhere take yaj├▒├бm as object. Moreover, one nominal form of v├н тИЪstс╣Ы, namely viс╣гс╣н├нraс╕е in II.13.10, does seem to have spatial force (JPB тАШfar-flungтАЩ). I donтАЩt have a good solution.

Griffith

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬNow, leaders (of the rains), they support (the world); now, blending together, they bear (the oblation) now, situated remote, (they uphold distant objects); so may their manifold forms be manifest.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

They uphold the distant objects: the text has only adh─Б par─Бvat─Б: the latter is formed from paravat, d┼лrade┼Ыaс╕е, a distant plural ce or country, tat sambandhinaс╕е being in relation to it; i.e., the winds being in the firmament give support to the distant stars and plural nets

Jamison Brereton

Then they vaunt themselves as тАЬmen (come) downтАЭ; then they vaunt themselves as тАЬteamsтАЭ;
then as тАЬthose from afar.тАЭ Their bright forms are worthy to be seen.

Jamison Brereton Notes

My interpr. of this vs. follows from that of 10 and diverges from those of others. By my interpr. the nom. plurals are further names the Maruts call themselves, shown most clearly by the ├нti ending p─Бda c. Most interpr. take c with d, syntactically and semantically divorced from ab – e.g., Klein (DGRV II.102-3, closely flg. Geldner) тАЬ(And) the men proclaim it (as worthy) and (their) teams proclaim (it so), and wondrous (are their) forms, worthy of being seen, (of whom they say,) тАЬ(They are) from the distance.тАЭ But the ├бdh─БтАЩs that open p─Бdas a, b, and c impose, or at least beg for, a parallel interpr. of the three p─Бdas, esp. with the ├нti closing the last, and the parenthetical тАЬ(of whom they say)тАЭ is ad hoc, generated only from the ├нti of c.

One of the problems not mentioned by the standard interpr. is the intrusive n├н in p─Бda a. The verb тИЪuh does not otherwise occur with this preverb, and since ohate is surrounded by identical forms without preverb (10d, 11b) it seems unlikely that only the middle one would have the preverb. It might be loosely inspired by the ni in niy├║ta(с╕е) in b, but ┼Ъy─Бv─Б┼Ыva does not seem the type of poet to throw in verbal fragments without function. I suggest rather that it continues but varies the naming pattern of 10ab with PREV-pathi-, here with the n├н a very minimalist predication of n├бraс╕е тАЬmen down.тАЭ

Griffith

To this the Heroes well attend, well do their teams attend to this.
Visible are their varied forms. Behold, they are Paravatas.

Die M├дnner, ja sie achten drauf und ihre Vielgespanne auch, Sie, die man aus der Ferne ruft, Gestalten pr├дchtig, sehenswerth.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬThe reciters of sacred metres, desirous of water, and celebrating (the Maruts), have drawn them to (provide) a well (for Gotama); some of them (invisible) as thieves, have been my defenders; some have been (obvious) to view through the light (of life).тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Chanting in rhythm, seeking water, (like) light-weights they pranced to the wellspring.
They (seemed indistinct) to me like who knows who, like thieves
(concealed), but the helpers (then) came to glitter in my sight.

Jamison Brereton Notes

This vs. bristles with difficulties. The first to present itself is the hapax kubhany├║-. There are several competing interpr. of this word, though Geldner refuses to tr.

it at all. Renou tr. тАЬvou├йs ├а un rite communiel,тАЭ which he derives from Benveniste (BSL 52 [1956] 11-12 [not yet seen by me]), who connected it with Ossetic material: see KEWA III.676; the Ossetic connection was disputed by Szemer├йnyi; see KEWA ref.

and EWA s.v., and seems in principle farfetched. Another, going back to Neisser (see EWA s.v.) and followed by Scarlatta (640) and Witzel Got┼Н, is тАШyelling, shoutingтАЩ, from тИЪbhan тАШspeakтАЩ, with the pejorative prefix ku-. (Remmer [Frauennamen, p. 48] also follows this basic analysis, but takes the ku- in positive sense: тАЬwelche Redner!тАЭ hence тАЬwortgewaltig.тАЭ) More likely is an analysis stemming ultimately from S─Бyaс╣Зa.тАЩs udakecchavaс╕е (see GeldnerтАЩs n. 12a тАЬWasser w├╝nschendтАЭ). Geldner cites similarly formed udany├бvaс╕е тАШwater seekingтАЩ in nearby V.54.2, 57.1 (latter also has an ├║tsa- тАШwellspringтАЩ as here). The Kubh─Б river also figures in this Marut cycle, in the next hymn V.53.9 in a list of river names. A derived adj. *kubh─Б-y├║- тАШseeking the Kubh─БтАЩ can easily have been formed. Given the common interchange of -─Б-y├б/├║- and -any├б/├║- derivatives (type vс╣Ыс╣г─Бy├б-, vс╣Ыс╣гaс╣Зy├б-), *kubh─Бy├║- could have been reformed as kubhany├║-, esp. under the influence of udany├║-; see also iс╣гaс╣Зyata in 14d. Here it can mean either тАШseeking the Kubh─Б RiverтАЩ or тАШseeking waterтАЩ more generally. Since their goal in the following p─Бda is a wellspring (├║tsam), seeking some sort of water source makes good sense in the passage.

The meaning of the word k─лr├н(n)- is disputed, with the two leading contenders тАШbardтАЩ and тАШweak, poorтАЩ. The former, the only sense given by Grassmann, seems to be currently in the ascendancy after eclipse – e.g., KEWA glosses it only as тАШgering, niedrig, armтАЩ, but EWA as тАШDichter, Lobs├дngerтАЩ, with тАШweakтАЩ banished to the small print – perhaps because it is easier to etymologize (тИЪkс╣Э тАШcelebrateтАЩ). But the contexts, esp. the fact that it is regularly followed by cid тАШevenтАЩ and often refers to a person receiving divine aid despite his condition, favor the latter. See also my brief disc. in Hyenas (251-52). The sense тАШweak, poorтАЩ fits our context less well, since the Maruts are powerful and outfitted with enough bling to make them rich. But if тАШweakтАЩ can be interpreted as тАШlightweight, light on their feetтАЩ, it can work: the Maruts are dancing to the wellspring. Another issue is the status of the stem k─лr├нn- to which this form is assigned. The only other forms possibly belonging to this stem are 3 instr. sg. k─лr├нс╣З─Б (I.100.9, V.4.10, 40.8), but they can also of course belong to the reasonably wellattested simple i-stem k─лr├н-. Mehendale (тАЬTwo Vedic Notes: (1) k─лr├нn?тАЭ BSOAS 1974: 670-71) attempts to eliminate the -├нn-stem entirely by analyzing our form as instr. sg. k─лr├нс╣З─Б + u, with u replacing the usual cid, and this interpr. is tentatively followed by Witzel Got┼Н. But u is hardly equivalent to cid and it is highly unlikely to be placed here, in the middle of a p─Бda and a clause. Our understanding of Rigvedic particle usage has advanced considerably since 1974. If we want to eliminate, or limit, k─лr├нn-, it should first be noted that of the three instr. sgs., two are in Maс╣Зс╕Нala V (V.4.10, 40.8), and so it is possible that the poets of V reinterpr. k─лr├нс╣З─Б as belonging to an -├нn-stem; there are no unambig. exx. of the plain i-stem k─лr├н- in V. Certainly there is no possessive sense associated with the putative k─лr├нn- forms as far as I can see.

The 2nd hemistich also presents difficulties: how to construe the indefinite expression k├й cid, why the Maruts are compared to/identified with thieves, and whether c and d form a single expression or two. These questions have been addressed in various ways in the standard transl.; I will treat only my own. My rendering assumes that c and d are separate clauses (contra the standard view) depicting a two-step process. For c I start with the fact that what thieves mostly do in the RV is hide. I assume that the Maruts are likened to thieves because on their first approach, enveloped in clouds perhaps, they are indistinct and unidentifiable; this is also conveyed by the indefinite k├й cin n├б тАЬlike who knows who.тАЭ (I do not take k├й cid directly with t─Бy├бvaс╕е, but interpr. them as two different ways of referring to the stealthy Maruts, again against most interpr.) In d the Maruts suddenly flash out (─Бsan dс╣Ы┼Ы├н tviс╣г├й тАЬcame to glitter in my sightтАЭ) as the storm, or specifically the lightning. As they become visible in this way, it also becomes clear that they are тАШhelpersтАЩ (┼л╠Бm─Бс╕е); as usual, the assumption behind this is that the storm, though violent, brings fructifying rain – rain which is previewed in the first hemistich, where the Maruts seek water and prance to the wellspring, while chanting in rhythm, presumably a reference to thunder.

Griffith

Hymn-singing, seeking water, they, praising, have danced about the spring.
What are they unto me? No thieves, but helpers, splendid to behold.

Geldner

Die liedersingenden ………Barden tanzten zu dem Brunnen. Die Helfer kamen mir zu Gesicht wie unbekannte Diebe zur ├Ьberraschung.

Grassmann

Lied singend, h├╝pfend tanzten sie her zu dem Born die jubelnden; Wie R├дuberbanden schienen sie geschart zum Andrang meinem Blick.

Elizarenkova

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬGlorify, с╣Ъс╣гi, with grateful praise, the company of the Maruts, who are manifest, bright with lightning lances, who are wise, and the creators (of all things).тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Which lofty ones, whose spears are lightning flashes, are (also) sage poets, ritual adeptsтАФ
to this Marut flock, o seer, do homage and bring it to a halt with song.

Jamison Brereton Notes

On the phrase с╣Ыс╣гv─Б╠Бс╣Ыс╣гс╣н├нvidyutaс╕е see disc. ad vs. 6; for the number disharmony in y├й тАж t├бm see disc. ad vs. 7; for the seemingly unnecessary copula s├бnti see disc. ad vs. 2 as well as immediately below.

This vs. serves as another boundary. The Maruts of the thunderstorm, dominating the middle of this hymn, are reconfigured as ritualists, appropriate guests and participants at our sacrifice. The ritual context now takes over for the rest of the hymn. This thematic transition may help explain the s├бnti. In p─Бda a the Maruts are still lofty ones with spears of lightning – untamed forces of nature – but in b they are asserted to be poets and ritual adepts (kav├бyaс╕е тАж vedh├бsaс╕е). Perhaps the s├бnti marks the two forms in b as predicate nouns in an equational sentence (X IS Y), where X and Y belong to very different domains.

The address or, as seems likely, self-address to the seer (rс╣гe) returns us to the very beginning of the hymn, with ┼Ъy─Бv─Б┼ЫvaтАЩs clear self-address in 1ab.

Griffith

Sublime, with lightnings for their spears, Sages and Orderers are they.
Rsi, adore that Marut host, and make them happy with thy song.

Geldner

Die speerblitzenden Recken, die Seher und Meister sind, vor dieser marutischen Schar verbeuge dich, o Rishi, und bring sie mit Lobreden zum Stillstand!

Grassmann

Die hohen Speer-ergl├дnzenden, die weise, treue Helfer sind, o S├дnger, diese Marutschar verehre, fessle durch dein Lied.

Elizarenkova

рд╣реЗ рдЛрд╖реЗ рдорд╛рд░реБрддрдВ рдЧрдгрдВ рдорд░реБрддреНрд╕рдВрдШрдВ рдорд┐рддреНрд░рдВ рди рдЖрджрд┐рддреНрдпрдорд┐рд╡ рджрд╛рдирд╛ рд╣рд╡рд┐рд░реНрджрд╛рдиреЗрди рдпреЛрд╖рдгрд╛ ред рдпреМрддреЗрд░рд┐рджрдВ рд░реВрдкрдореН ред рдпреМрддреАрддрд┐ рдпреЛрд╖рд╛ рд╕реНрддреБрддрд┐рдГ ред рддрдпрд╛ рдЪ рдЕрдЪреНрдЫ рдЕрднрд┐рдЧрдЪреНрдЫреЗрддрд┐ рд╢реЗрд╖рдГ ред рдЛрд╖реЗрд░реБрддреНрддрд░рд╛рд░реНрдзрдГ рдкреНрд░рддреНрдпрдХреНрд╖рд╡рд╛рджрдГ ред рдУрдЬрд╕рд╛ рдмрд▓реЗрди рд╣реЗ рдзреГрд╖реНрдгрд╡рдГ рдзрд░реНрд╖рдХрд╛ рдорд░реБрддрдГ рджрд┐рд╡реЛ рд╡рд╛ рджреНрдпреБрд▓реЛрдХрд╛рджреНрд╡рд╛ ред рд╡рд╛рд╢рдмреНрджрд╢реНрд░реБрддреЗрдГ рдЗрддрд░рд▓реЛрдХрджреНрд╡рдпрд╛рджреНрд╡рд╛ ред рдзреАрднрд┐рдГ рдЕрд╕реНрдорджреАрдпрд╛рднрд┐рдГ рд╕реНрддреБрддрд┐рднрд┐рдГ рд╕реНрддреБрддрд╛рдГ рдЗрд╖рдгреНрдпрдд рдЧрдЪреНрдЫрдд рдпрдЬреНрдЮрдореН рее

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬApproach, с╣Ъс╣гi, with offerings and with praise, the company of the Maruts like a friend; come, sustaining (Maruts), with your strength, from heaven of (any other region), glorified by our hymns.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Like a friend: mitram na may also be rendered ─Бdityam iva, like the sun

Jamison Brereton

To the Marut flock, o seer, (approach) with a gift, as a maiden being given (in marriage) (approaches) her ally [=spouse?].
Or from heaven do you, bold ones, praised with poetic thoughts, speed with strength.

Jamison Brereton Notes

The self-address of 13c seems important enough to repeat here in p─Бda with minimal variation, though the syntactic function of the acc. m─Б╠Бrutam gaс╣З├бm is different and the rest of the vs. much less clear.

The first hemistich lacks a verb; the parameters of what to supply are set by the nominal arguments in a – the seer is commanded (/commands himself) to [DO SOMETHING] to(ward) (├бcha) the Marut flock – and further limited by the simile in b, with the nom. maiden (yoс╣г├бс╣З─Б) roughly corresponding to the seer and the acc. friend/ally (mitr├бm) to the Maruts. I have supplied тАШapproachтАЩ, others тАШinvite, address, turnтАЩ, etc., all more or less acceptable.

The question then is what the simile in b is conveying. Most of the renderings attribute bolder action to the maiden than I think gently bred Vedic girls would ordinarily undertake (see esp. Klein, DGRV II.183-84: тАЬтАж like a maiden entices a friendтАЭ). My solution is to read d─Бn─Б╠Бtwice in two different morphological interpr.

First, with the standard interpr., as the instr. sg. of тАШgiftтАЩ (on the possible stems, see EWA s.v. d─Бn├б-). But also as a root aor. mid. participle in the nom. sg. fem. with passive value. Although such a participle is not recognized by the standard grammars, it is exactly the form we would expect and fits the gift-marriage model perfectly. The mitr├б- to whom she is given is presumably her spouse; on mitr├б- in a wedding context see X.27.12 and my тАЬThe Rigvedic Svayaс╣ГvaraтАЭ (Fs. Parpola 2001), 309-13.

The final word of b, yoс╣г├бс╣З─Б, is anomalously accented (vs. standard y├│с╣гaс╣З─Б).

See below comm. ad 15b for a possible explanation. The second hemistich seems to be presented as a disjunctive alternative to the first, introduced by v─Б. The тАЬorтАЭ does not make much sense; it is tempting to follow RenouтАЩs judgment: тАЬv─Б irrationnel.тАЭ But Klein (II.184) may have rightly divined the rationale: тАЬthe poet first beseeches the Rishi to entice the Maruts to the worship, but then, as an alternative, appeals directly to the Maruts themselves to come.тАЭ I would tweak this slightly by suggesting that the action to which 14cd is presented as an alternative is not 14ab, but rather 13cd, of which 14a(b) is a variant. The с╣Ыс╣гi orders himself to stop the Maruts with a song (13cd) but then suggests to them that they initiate the journey themselves (14cd).

The voc. dhс╣Ыс╣гс╣Зavaс╕е addressed to the Maruts again reminds us of the beginning of the hymn, with dhс╣Ыс╣гс╣Зuy─Б╠Б(1a, 2b, 4b) and dhс╣Ыс╣гadv├нnaс╕е (2c).

Griffith

Rsi, invite the Marut band with offerings, as a maid her friend.
From heaven, too, Bold Ones, in your might haste hither glorified with songs.

Geldner

Lade, o Rishi, die marutische Schar mit Gabe ein wie die junge Frau einen Freund. Oder eilet mit Macht vom Himmel her, ihr Mutigen, mit Gedichten gepriesen!

Grassmann

Auf, S├дnger, hin zur Marutschar mit Gaben wie zum Freund die Braut; Ihr k├╝hnen eilt vom Himmel her, gepries’ne kr├дftig, eifervoll.

Elizarenkova

English translation:

тАЬGlorifying them promptly, desiring not to bring (other) deities to (his) presence, let (the worshipper) associate his gifts with those wise (divinities) renowned for their velocity, and distributors (of rewards).тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Now (a man) paying mind to them, (who approaches) to the gods as if to udders,
he would keep company with a gift, through (the auspices of) the
patrons famed on the course [=Maruts] and by their unguents.

Jamison Brereton Notes

This vs. is a variant of 14, with the parts somewhat differently distributed.

The phrase dev─Б╠Бm╠Р├бch─Б in b resembles ├бcha тАж m─Б╠Бrutaс╣Г gaс╣З├бm in 14a, and it therefore seems prudent and economical to supply the same verb as in 14a.

Although in 14ab d─Бn─Б╠Бbelonged to the same syntagm as ├бcha тАж m─Б╠Бrutaс╣Г gaс╣З├бm, here it is construed with a different part of the sentence, with the opt. saceta тАШwould/might/could keep companyтАЩ. In 14 the poet was offering a gift to the Maruts; here he тАЬkeeps company with a giftтАЭ – that is, receives it – bestowed by the Maruts.

The situation is the standard reciprocal exchange of praise and worship for the gods for material benefits from the gods. The givers are first identified as s┼лr├н-s тАШpatronsтАЩ (c), and one could think of the human patrons often so called, but p─Бda d makes it clear that the Maruts are meant, and the identification of the s┼лr├бyaс╕е with the Maruts is even clearer in 16b.

The two instr. in d are off balance: y─Б╠Бma┼Ыrutebhiс╕е тАШfamed on/by their course/journeyтАЩ modifies the Maruts, but, pace Grassmann, Geldner, and Witzel Got┼Н, a├▒j├нbhiс╕е should not, because a├▒j├н- is only a noun тАШunguent, adornmentтАЩ (see in the next hymn V.53.4), not the adj. their tr. require. Renou recognizes the problem and suggests that it is an тАЬinstrumental of identificationтАЭ: тАЬen tant que (porteurs dтАЩ) ornements.тАЭ I think rather that y─Б╠Бma- and a├▒j├нbhiс╕е are functionally parallel, both to be construed with ┼Ыrut├б-, but one in a cmpd and one in an independent syntagm. For similar interplay between cmpd member and independent word, see comm. ad VIII.1.2.

The real problem in this vs. is vakс╣г├бс╣З─Б. In the published translation I follow Geldner and Renou in taking it as an acc. pl. of vakс╣г├бс╣З─Б тАШudderтАЩ, but of course this stem is fem. and the acc. pl. form here should be vakс╣г├бс╣З─Бс╕е. Geldner (n. 15b) casually suggests that it is exceptionally neuter or else a mistake for vakс╣г├бс╣З─Бс╕е, Renou that itтАЩs a тАЬnt. insolite.тАЭ Others provide different morphological analysis: Grassmann sets up a special stem vakс╣г├бс╣З─Б тАШDarbringungтАЩ and must take it as a nom. sg.; Oldenberg suggests emending the accent to

*v├бkс╣гaс╣З─Б, allowing it to belong to the stem v├бkс╣гaс╣Зa- тАШstrengtheningтАЩ and takes it as a neut. nom. pl. (тАЬwie zu den G├╢ttern die St├дrkungenтАЭ); Witzel Got┼Н maintain the тАШudderтАЩ analysis but take it as a nom. sg.: тАЬDer тАж (wendet) sich den g├╢ttlichen (Maruts) zu wie ein Schlauch (der gef├╝llt sein will).тАЭ This last is the most ingenious and does the least violence to the morphology / repertoire of stems, but the image is an odd one, to say the least. My explanation, admittedly rather weak, starts from the similar patterning of vss. 14 and 15: 1) the ├бcha + acc. gods noted above (though ├бcha differently positioned), in each case requiring a verb to be supplied; 2) d─Бn─Б╠Б(beg. of 14b/15c); 3) the parallel endings of the b p─Бdas: 14b тАж n├б yoс╣г├бn─Б / 15c тАж n├б vakс╣г├бn─Б. The final word of each of these p─Бdas is problematic: yoс╣г├бс╣З─Б has the wrong accent, vakс╣г├бс╣З─Б has the wrong ending. I suggest that the words were mutually adjusted to each other, either in composition or redactionally. Oldenberg already suggested (in his n. 2) that yoс╣г├бс╣З─Б might owe its accent to vakс╣г├бс╣З─Б, but the suggestion was halfhearted since he really wanted to emend the accent of vakс╣г├бс╣З─Б to *v├бkс╣гaс╣З─Б, as I just noted. However, this seems the best explanation of the accent of yoс╣г├бс╣З─Б, and conversely this allows us also to assume that acc. pl. *vakс╣г├бс╣З─Бс╕е lost its -с╕е to match yoс╣г├бn─Б. Although this may seem no different from GeldnerтАЩs and RenouтАЩs arbitrary conferral of neut. gender, my explanation is contextually tied and has some possibility of being correct.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬTo me, inquiring of their kindred, the sage (Maruts) have uttered a reply; they have declaree Pс╣Ыс╣гс╣Зi (to be their) mother; the mighty ones have declared the food-bestowing Rudra (to be their) father.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Seven times seven: there are seven toops of Maruts, each consisting of seven, making up the number of forty-nine

Jamison Brereton

Those who proclaimed the cow to me on my seeking (their) lineage, the patrons called Pr╠е┼Ыni their mother,
then they called their father arrow-possessing RudraтАФ(they) the
skillful ones.

Jamison Brereton Notes

This Paс╣Еkti vs. is the last real vs. of the hymn, since 17 (also Paс╣Еkti) is a d─Бnastuti. It begins with pr├б, just as vs. 1 did, and continues with the insistent repetion of the verb of speech vocanta (p─Бdas b, c, e). The vs. is also reminiscent of repeated ohate тАШvaunt themselvesтАЩ in 10-11; as there, the recipient of the MarutsтАЩ speech here is тАЬme.тАЭ The structure of the vs. would be clearer if the tr. read тАЬThose who proclaimed тАж they proclaimed P. their mother, then they proclaimed their father тАжтАЭ On iс╣гm├нn- see comm. ad I.87.6.

Griffith

Princes, who, when I asked their kin, named Prsni as their Mother-cow,
And the impetuous Rudra they, the Mighty Ones, declared their Sire.

Geldner

Die Herren, die mir bei der Nachforschung nach ihrer Sippe die Kuh nannten, die Prisni als ihre Mutter nannten, die nannten dann als ihren Vater den pfeilf├╝hrenden Rudra, sie die Kundigen.

Grassmann

Die, als ich nach der Sippschaft frug, als Mutter nannten Pri├зni mir, als Vater, glanzvoll, kr├дftig sie, den schnellen St├╝rmer Rudra mir.

Elizarenkova

рд╕рдкреНрдд рд╕рдкреНрддрд╕рдВрдЦреНрдпрд╛рдХрд╛рдГ рд╕рдВрдШрд╛рдГ ред рд╕рдкреНрддрдЧрдгрд╛ рд╡реИ рдорд░реБрддрдГ ’ (рддреИ. рд╕рдВ. реи. реи. резрез. рез ) рдЗрддрд┐ рд╢реНрд░реБрддреЗрдГ ред рдЕрджрд┐рддрд┐рдЧрд░реНрднреЗ рд╡рд░реНрддрдорд╛рдирдВ рд╡рд╛рдпреБрдорд┐рдиреНрджреНрд░рдГ рдкреНрд░рд╡рд┐рд╢реНрдп рд╕рдкреНрддрдзрд╛ рд╡рд┐рджрд╛рд░реНрдп рдкреБрдирд░реЗрдХреИрдХрдВ рд╕рдкреНрддрдзрд╛ рд╡реНрдпрджрд╛рд░рдпрддреН рддреЗ рдПрдХреЛрдирдкрдЮреНрдЪрд╛рд╢рдиреНрдорд░реБрджреНрдЧрдгрд╛ рдЕрднрд╡рдиреНрдирд┐рддрд┐ рдкреБрд░рд╛рдгреЗрд╖реБ рдкреНрд░рд╕рд┐рджреНрдзрдореН ред рддреЗ рдЪ рд╕рдкреНрддрд╕рдВрдЦреНрдпрд╛рдХрд╛рдГ рд╢рд╛рдХрд┐рдирдГ рд╕рд░реНрд╡рдордкрд┐ рдХрд░реНрддреБрдВ рд╢рдХреНрддрд╛рдГ ред рддреЗ рдЪ рдПрдХрдореЗрдХрд╛ рдПрдХреИрдХреЛ рдЧрдгрдГ рдореЗ рдорд╣реНрдпрдВ рд╢рддрд╛ рд╢рддрд╕рдВрдЦреНрдпрд╛рдХрд╛рдирд┐ рдЧрд╡рд╛рд╢реНрд╡рдпреВрдерд╛рдирд┐ рджрджреБрдГ рджрддреНрддрд╡рдиреНрддрдГред рдкреНрд░рдпрдЪреНрдЫрдиреНрддреНрд╡рд┐рддрд┐ рд╡рд╛ рдЖрд╢реАрдГ ред рддреИрд░реНрджрддреНрддрдВ рдпрдореБрдирд╛рдпрд╛рдВ рдирджреНрдпрд╛рдореН рдЕрдзрд┐ ред рдЕрдпрдВ рд╕рдкреНрддрдореНрдпрд░реНрдерд╛рдиреБрд╡рд╛рджреА ред рддрддреНрд░ рд╢реНрд░реБрддрдВ рдкреНрд░рд╕рд┐рджреНрдзрдВ рдЧрд╡реНрдпрдВ рдЧреЛрд╕рдореВрд╣рд╛рддреНрдордХрдВ рдЧреЛрд╕рдВрдмрдиреНрдзрд┐ рд╡рд╛ рд░рд╛рдзрдГ рдзрдирдореН рдЙрддреН рдореГрдЬреЗ рдЙрдиреНрдорд╛рд░реНрдЬрдпрд╛рдорд┐ ред рддрдерд╛ рддреИрд░реНрджрддреНрддрдореН рдЕрд╢реНрд╡реНрдпрдореН рдЕрд╢реНрд╡рд╕рдореВрд╣рд╛рддреНрдордХрдВ рддрддреНрд╕рдВрдмрдиреНрдзрд┐ рд╡рд╛ рд░рд╛рдзрдГ рдзрдирдВ рдирд┐ рдореГрдЬреЗ рдирд┐рдорд╛рд░реНрдЬреНрдорд┐ рее рее резреж рее

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬMay the seven times seven all-potent (Maruts, aggregated as) a single troop, bestow upon me hundreds (of cattle) may I possess wealth of cows, renowned upon the (banks of) the Yamun─Б; may I possess wealth of horses.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Upon the banks of Yamun─Б: yamun─Бy─Бm adhi ┼Ыrutam r─Бdho gavyam: an extraordinary allusion anticipating Gokula of Kс╣Ыс╣гс╣Зa

Jamison Brereton

Seven upon seven the able ones gave me hundreds, one (hundred) each. At the Yamun─Б (River) a famous thingтАФI swept up bounty in cattle; swept down bounty in horses.

Jamison Brereton Notes

By all standard interpr. the Maruts are the subjects of this d─Бnastuti, but it is worth noting that they are not named – and so it is possible that a set of human patrons, assimilated to the Maruts and thus endowed with their prestige, are the actual donors praised.

Note the etymological chaining between the subj. of 16e ┼Ы├нkvasaс╕е and 17a ┼Ы─Бk├нnaс╕е, both deriv. from тИЪ┼Ыak. This could be evidence of the identity of the subjects (Maruts both), or it could be another way of conferring Marut qualities on the human patrons.

The unbalanced ─Бmreс╕Нita ├йkam-ek─Б is curiously formed. AiG III.395 suggests that the pl. ek─Б has been attracted to the following ┼Ыat─Б╠Б, whose attribute it is. It also seems an attempt, utilizing both sg. ├йkam and pl. ek─Б, to express the awkward distributive, of one hundred per each of seven Maruts, producing a total of plural hundreds.

Griffith

The mighty ones, the seven times seven, have singly given me hundred gifts.
I have obtained on Yamuna famed wealth in kine and wealth in steeds.

Geldner

Die je sieben und sieben M├дchten gaben mir je einhundert K├╝he. An der Yamuna bekomme ich als Ehrenanteil die ber├╝hmte Schenkung von K├╝hen, streiche ich die Schenkung von Rossen ein.

Elizarenkova

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рд╡рд┐рд╖рдпрдГ

рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдерд╛рдиреНрд╡рдпрднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - (рд╕рдкреНрдд) рд╕рдкреНрддрд╡рд┐рдзрд╛ рдорд░реБрджреНрдЧрдгрд╛ рдордиреБрд╖реНрдпрднреЗрджрд╛рдГ (рдореЗ) рдордо (рд╕рдкреНрдд) (рд╢рд╛рдХрд┐рдирдГ) рд╢рдХреНрддрд┐рдордиреНрддрдГ (рдПрдХрдореЗрдХрд╛) рдПрдХрдореЗрдХрд╛рдирд┐ (рд╢рддрд╛) рд╢рддрд╛рдирд┐ (рджрджреБрдГ) рдкреНрд░рдпрдЪреНрдЫреЗрдпреБрдГ (рдпрдореБрдирд╛рдпрд╛рдореН) рдпрдордирд┐рдпрдорд╛рдиреНрд╡рд┐рддрд╛рдпрд╛рдВ рдХреНрд░рд┐рдпрд╛рдпрд╛рдореН (рдЕрдзрд┐) (рд╢реНрд░реБрддрдореН) (рдЙрддреН) (рд░рд╛рдзрдГ) рдзрдирдореН (рдЧрд╡реНрдпрдореН) рдЧреЛрд╣рд┐рддрдореН (рдореГрдЬреЗ) рд╢реБрдиреНрдзрд╛рдорд┐ (рдирд┐) рдирд┐рддрд░рд╛рдореН (рд░рд╛рдзрдГ) рджреНрд░рд╡реНрдпрдореН (рдЕрд╢реНрд╡реНрдпрдореН) рдЕрд╢реНрд╡реЗрд╖реБ рд╕рд╛рдзреБ (рдореГрдЬреЗ) рд╢реБрдиреНрдзрд╛рдорд┐ реерезренрее

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдердГ

рд╕рд╡рд┐рддрд╛ рдЬреЛрд╢реА тЖР рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рдо) - рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдердГ
